Property Found with a Foundling: The Ruling on Tied Money
Ruling on property found with foundling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on money tied to a foundling and identify the condition that establishes ownership.

Core Idea
Money tied to a foundling is his property due to the apparent sign of attachment.

This lesson deals with a specific case: when a foundling (abandoned child) is found with money physically tied to him. The text provides a clear ruling based on the principle of apparent signs (al-ʿalāmah al-ẓāhirah). Understanding this helps distinguish found property from the foundling's own assets and clarifies when the sign alone is sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Identify the person: the foundling (laqīṭ) – an abandoned child whose lineage is unknown.
The ruling presumes the child is a free Muslim, but the principle applies generally.
2
Identify the object
Identify the object: money (māl) that is found physically tied onto the foundling.
The attachment must be physical (mashdūd ʿalayhi), not just nearby.
3
Recognize the sign
Recognize that the tied state is an apparent sign (ʿalāmah ẓāhirah) indicating ownership.
Hanafi fiqh treats such signs as strong indicators in absence of contradictory evidence.
4
Apply the principle
Apply the general principle: in the absence of an opposing claimant, judgement is based on the apparent sign.
The text references an earlier rule: 'if there is no opponent, judgement will be made on the sign.'
5
State the ruling
State the final ruling: the tied money belongs to the foundling, to be used for his care.
The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the muftā bihī position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان وجد مع اللقيط مال مشدود عليه فهو له (١٠)
[۱۶۱۶) (۹) اگر لقیط کے ساتھ مال باندھا ہوا پایا گیا تو وہ مال اسی کا ہے۔
لقیط کے ساتھ بندھا ہوا ہونا دلیل ہے کہ یہ مال لقیط ہی کا ہے۔ اس لئے اس علامت ظاہرہ کی وجہ سے مال لقیط کا ہوگا۔ پہلے گزر گیا ہے کہ کوئی مزاحم نہ ہو تو علامت پر فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ یہاں بھی ایسا ہی ہے۔
(10) And if money is found with the foundling tied onto him, it belongs to him. [1616] (9) If money tied is found with the foundling, then that money is his. Being tied with the foundling is evidence that this money belongs to the foundling. Therefore due to this apparent sign, the money will be the foundling's. It has passed earlier that if there is no opponent, judgement will be made on the sign. Here it is similar.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This ruling concerns property found physically attached to the foundling. The text states that if money (māl) is found tied onto the foundling (mashdūd ʿalayhi), it belongs to him. The Urdu commentary explains that the fact that it is tied to him is a clear sign (ʿalāmah ẓāhirah) that the money is his property. This is consistent with the earlier principle that in the absence of any opposing claimant, judgement is based on apparent signs. Therefore, the finder (multaqiṭ) or the authorities should consider that money as the foundling's property, to be used for his benefit.

Key Terms
مال (māl): Property; money or valuables.
علامت ظاہرہ (ʿalāmah ẓāhirah): Apparent sign; external evidence that leads to a legal presumption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a foundling is found with a bag of coins tied around his waist, who owns the money?
A) The finder of the child.
B) The state treasury (bayt al-māl).
C) The foundling himself.
D) The previous owner, if found.

Key Takeaway
Money physically tied to a foundling is his property due to the apparent sign of attachment, in the absence of any opposing claimant.

Limitations on the Finder's Disposition of Foundling's Property
Limitations on finder's disposition of foundling's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the finder's disposition of the foundling's property and distinguish between permissible and impermissible uses.

Core Idea
The finder may only spend on necessities; trading without need is prohibited.

This lesson examines the limits of the finder's (multaqiṭ) authority over the property of a foundling (laqīṭ). The Hanafi school strictly restricts the finder's right to dispose of the foundling's wealth to only what is necessary for the child's immediate needs. Any transaction beyond that, such as trade, is invalid because the finder lacks guardianship (wilāyah) over the property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the Arabic text: the finder is not to dispose of the foundling's property. The general ruling is that disposition (taṣarruf) is not permissible (lā yajūz).
Note the negative particle 'lā' indicating prohibition.
2
Note the exception for necessities
The Urdu commentary clarifies that the finder may purchase food, clothing, and necessities from the foundling's money. These are allowed because they are essential for the child's survival.
The exception is based on the principle of necessity (ḍarūrah).
3
Understand the rationale for prohibition of trade
The text explicitly says the finder cannot engage in buying and selling (trade) because there is no need for it. The finder lacks the authority (wilāyah) to use the property for non-essential purposes.
The underlying reason is the preservation of the foundling's wealth.
4
Recognize the consequence of unauthorized disposition
If the finder trades without necessity, the transaction is invalid (bāṭil). The finder may become liable for any loss, as he acted without authority.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle that acts beyond one's legal capacity are void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١١١٦١٨) ولا تصرفه في مال اللقيط ( ١٦١٩ (١٢)
[۱۶۱۸) (۱۱) اور نہیں جائز ہے لقیط کے مال میں تصرف کرنا۔
لقیط کے لئے لقیط کے مال سے کھانا، کپڑا اور ضروریات زندگی ملتقط خرید سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اس کے مال کو خرید و فروخت میں ڈال کر خرد برد نہیں کر سکتا ہے اس کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور بلاوجہ کی چیز میں نقطہ کے مال کو ڈالنے کی متفقط کو ولایت نہیں ہے۔
(11) And he (the finder) is not to dispose of the foundling's property. (12) [1618] (11) And it is not permissible to dispose of the foundling's property. The finder can purchase food, clothing, and necessities of life for the foundling from his property. But he cannot trade with his property, buying and selling, because there is no need for that, and the finder has no authority to put the foundling's property into something unnecessary.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This ruling clarifies the finder's limited authority over the foundling's property. The text states that the finder (multaqiṭ) is not allowed to dispose (taṣarruf) of the foundling's property. The Urdu commentary explains that the finder may use the property to buy necessary items like food, clothing, and other essentials for the foundling. However, he cannot engage in trade (buying and selling) with the foundling's money, as there is no necessity (ḍarūrah) for such transactions, and the finder lacks the authority (wilāyah) to do so. This restriction ensures that the foundling's property is preserved and used only for his immediate needs.

Key Terms
تصرف (taṣarruf): Disposition; legal act involving property, such as sale, purchase, or gift.
ضرورة (ḍarūrah): Necessity; a pressing need that permits otherwise prohibited acts.
ولاية (wilāyah): Legal authority or guardianship over a person or property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can the finder use the foundling's money to start a small business for the foundling's future benefit?
A) Yes, because it is beneficial.
B) Yes, but only with court permission.
C) No, because it is not a necessity.
D) No, because the property belongs to the finder.

Key Takeaway
The finder's authority over the foundling's property is limited to necessities; any commercial transaction is invalid.

Finder's Authority over Foundling's Wealth
Rulings on the finder's disposal of the foundling's property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the limits of the finder's authority over the foundling's property and distinguish between permissible and impermissible actions.

Core Idea
The finder may only act for the foundling's benefit, not for speculation.

This lesson clarifies the boundaries of the finder's (multaqit) control over the foundling's (laqit) wealth. While the finder must provide necessities, he cannot use the wealth for trade or investment. The underlying principle is that all actions must serve the foundling's benefit. Understanding this limit is crucial to fulfilling the duty of care without overstepping legal boundaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the finder's disposal of the foundling's wealth. The ruling is that it is restricted to beneficial acts only.
The passage states clearly that the finder has no guardianship for unnecessary things.
2
List the permissible actions
The text explicitly mentions: buying food, clothing, and necessities; accepting gifts on behalf of the foundling; teaching him a craft; hiring him out for work.
These are all actions that directly benefit the foundling.
3
List the impermissible actions
The finder may not use the foundling's wealth for buying and selling (speculation) or any wasteful expenditure without need.
The principle is that the finder cannot take risks with the foundling's property.
4
Understand the governing principle
All permitted actions must be for the foundling's benefit (maslahah). Any harmful or unnecessary act is not allowed.
This principle distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from other schools that may grant broader authority.
5
Apply to a new scenario
Consider: can the finder invest the foundling's money in a fixed deposit? According to the Hanafi ruling, this is impermissible because it involves risk and is not a direct necessity.
The finder must avoid anything resembling trade or speculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب اللقيط (١١١٦١٨) ولا تصرفه في مال اللقيط. لقیط کے لئے لقیط کے مال سے کھانا، کپڑا اور ضروریات زندگی ملتقط خرید سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اس کے مال کو خرید و فروخت میں ڈال کر خرد برد نہیں کر سکتا ہے اس کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور بلاوجہ کی چیز میں نقطہ کے مال کو ڈالنے کی متفقط کو ولایت نہیں ہے۔ (١٦١٩) (١٢) ويجوز ان يقبض له الهبة ويسلمه في صناعة ويواجره. یہ مسئلہ اس قاعدے پر ہے کہ لقیط کے فائدے کے لئے ملتقط کام کر سکتا ہے۔ مثلا لفظ کے لئے جو ہبہ آئے اس پر قبضہ کرے یا لقیط کو کسی ہنر میں لگائے تا کہ اس سے نفع آئے۔ یا خود لقیط کو مزدوری پر لگائے تاکہ اس کی اجرت آئے اور لقیط پر خرچ کی جاسکے۔ یہ سب کام لقط کے فائدے کے لئے ہیں اس لئے یہ سب کام پانے والا کر سکتا ہے۔ الص لقیط کے لئے فائدے کا کام پانے والا کر سکتا ہے۔ نقصان کا کام نہیں کر سکتا۔
Chapter of the Foundling. (1618) And he does not have authority to dispose of the foundling's wealth. The finder may buy food, clothing, and necessities for the foundling from his wealth. But he may not put his wealth into buying and selling [speculation] because there is no need for that, and the finder has no guardianship to put the foundling's wealth into unnecessary things. (1619) (12) And it is permissible for him to accept a gift on his behalf, to train him in a craft, and to hire him out. This matter is based on the principle that the finder may act for the foundling's benefit. For example, he may accept a gift intended for the foundling, or teach him a skill to earn profit, or hire him out so that his wages come and can be spent on the foundling. All these actions are for the foundling's benefit, therefore the finder may do them. Summary: The finder may do beneficial acts for the foundling; he may not do harmful acts.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on the authority of the finder (multaqit) over the foundling's property. It is a ruling statement: the finder is not permitted to use the foundling's wealth for trade or speculation without necessity; he may only purchase essentials like food and clothing. However, he may accept gifts on the foundling's behalf, teach him a craft, or hire him out for work—all of which are beneficial. The underlying principle is that the finder acts for the foundling's benefit (maslahah). Any harmful or wasteful use is prohibited. This aligns with the Hanafi position that the finder has limited guardianship over the foundling's affairs.

Key Terms
لقیط (laqīṭ): A foundling, an abandoned child of unknown parentage.
ملتقط (multaqiṭ): The person who picks up and takes responsibility for the foundling.
صناعة (ṣināʿa): A craft or trade taught to the foundling for earning a living.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the finder (multaqit) permitted to do with the foundling's property?
A) Use it for trade and investment to increase profit.
B) Purchase only food, clothing, and necessities, and accept gifts on his behalf.
C) Use it for his own personal expenses.
D) Give it away as charity.

Key Takeaway
The finder's authority over the foundling's wealth is limited to actions that bring direct benefit, such as providing necessities and accepting gifts; speculative or unnecessary disposal is prohibited.

Luqata as Amanah with Witness
Ruling that luqata is a trust if finder makes witnesses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of luqata and identify the condition of witnesses that makes it a trust (amanah) in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Luqata is a trust only with witnesses; without it, the finder is liable.

In Hanafi fiqh, lost property (luqata) is not automatically a trust (amanah) in the finder's hands. The finder must take a specific step to protect himself from liability: he must make witnesses (ashhada) that he is taking the item to preserve and return it. This ruling, based on a hadith of the Prophet (ﷺ), balances the duty to safeguard lost property with the need to prevent neglect. This lesson unpacks that condition and its legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that the act is picking up lost property (luqata). The legal ruling depends on what the finder does next.
2
State the default ruling
Without any action, luqata is not automatically a trust. The finder could be liable if the item is damaged or lost.
3
State the condition
The finder must make witnesses (ishhad) at the time of picking up, declaring that he is taking it to preserve and return it.
The witnesses can be any two reliable Muslims or one man and two women (by Hanafi witness rules).
4
State the consequence
With witnesses, the luqata becomes a trust (amanah) in the finder's hand, meaning he is not liable for accidental damage or loss unless he is negligent.
5
Contrast without witnesses
If the finder does not make witnesses, the luqata is not a trust; the finder becomes a guarantor (damin) liable for any loss or damage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۰](١) اللقطة امانة فى يد الملتقط اذا اشهد الملتقط انه يأخذها ليحفظها ويرده على صاحبها.
Luqata is a trust in the hand of the finder when the finder makes witnesses that he is taking it to preserve it and return it to its owner.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of the chapter on Luqata. It establishes the fundamental principle: lost property (luqata) is classified as a trust (amanah) in the hand of the finder (multaqit), provided that the finder has witnesses (ashhada) to his act of taking it with the intention of preservation and return. This witness requirement protects the finder from liability; without it, the finder may become a guarantor. The condition of having witnesses is derived from the hadith of 'Iyad ibn Himar (mentioned in the Urdu commentary) where the Prophet commands witnessing upon finding a luqata. The ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
لقطة (luqata): Lost property picked up by someone other than its owner.
ملتقط (multaqit): The person who finds and picks up the lost property (luqata).
اشهاد (ishhad): The act of making witnesses to the fact that one is taking the lost property for preservation and return.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, under what condition does the luqata become a trust (amanah) in the hand of the finder?
A) When the finder announces it in the market.
B) When the finder makes witnesses that he is taking it to preserve and return it.
C) When the finder takes it with the intention to return it but does not tell anyone.
D) When the finder estimates its value correctly.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, luqata becomes a trust (amanah) only if the finder makes witnesses; without witnesses, the finder is a guarantor.

Announcement Periods for Lost Items (Luqata)
Ruling on the period of announcement based on value and disposal after period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the announcement period for luqata based on value and explain the finder's obligation after the period.

Core Idea
Lost items under ten dirhams require short announcement; valuable items require a full year.

In this lesson, we examine the second ruling of the chapter on luqata: how long must the finder announce a lost item? The Hanafi school distinguishes between small and large amounts based on the likelihood of the owner searching. After the announcement period, if the owner does not appear, the finder must give the item in charity. Let's study the matn's precise words.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two value thresholds
The text divides lost items based on value: 'less than ten dirhams' and 'ten dirhams or more'. Dirham is a silver coin; this is a legal criterion.
The threshold is ten dirhams; items of equal value (e.g., gold equivalent) follow the same rule.
2
Assign the announcement period
For less than ten dirhams, announce for 'ayyaman' (days); the minimum is three days per hadith. For ten dirhams or more, announce for 'hawlan kamilan' (a full year). The period must be continuous and complete.
The year is lunar; gaps may require restarting.
3
State the consequence after the period
After the period, if the owner appears, return the item. Otherwise, 'tasaddaq biha' (give it in charity). This charity is wajib and given on behalf of the owner.
If the finder keeps the item, he becomes a guarantor and must replace it if the owner appears.
4
Identify the legal status
Both the announcement and the charity are wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, based on the evidence from hadith.
This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۱](۲) فان كانت اقل من عشرة دراهم عرفها اياما وان كان عشرة فصاعدا عرفها حولا كاملا فان جاء صاحبها والا تصدق بها.
If it is less than ten dirhams, he announces it for days; and if it is ten or more, he announces it for a complete year. Then if its owner comes (he gives it to him), otherwise he gives it in charity.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This is the second ruling of the chapter on Luqata. The matn distinguishes between items of different value: if the lost item is worth less than ten dirhams (a relatively small amount), the finder should announce it for a few days. The minimum for this period is three days, as indicated in the hadith of Ya'la ibn Murrah cited in the Urdu commentary. If it is ten dirhams or more (or its equivalent), he must announce it for a full year. This differentiation is based on the likelihood of the owner searching for it; more valuable items are searched longer. After the announcement period, if the owner appears, the finder returns the item. If not, the finder must give it in charity. This charity is given on behalf of the owner, and if the owner later appears, the finder should compensate him or the reward of the charity is given to the owner. The Hanafi position is that it is wajib (obligatory) to give the item in charity after the year if the owner is not found. The finder cannot keep it for his own use without becoming a guarantor.

Key Terms
درهم (dirham): A silver coin used as a unit of currency; ten dirhams is the threshold for distinguishing between small and large lost items.
عرفها (arrafaha): He announces it; the act of making the lost item known publicly so that the owner may identify it.
حولا كاملا (hawlan kamilan): A complete year (one lunar year) of continuous announcement.
تصدق بها (tasaddaq biha): He gives it in charity; after the announcement period, the finder must give the item to the poor on behalf of the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should the finder do with a lost item worth less than ten dirhams after the announcement period if the owner does not appear?
A) Keep it for himself after one year.
B) Give it in charity.
C) Continue announcing for another year.
D) Sell it and keep the money.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling requires announcement for a few days for items under ten dirhams and a full year for items of ten dirhams or more, followed by charity if the owner does not appear.

Khuntha: Definition and Gender Determination by Urination
Defines khuntha and establishes urination as the gender determinant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of khuntha and apply the rule for determining its gender based on the source of urination.

Core Idea
A khuntha's gender is determined by the orifice from which urine flows—the first to release decides.

The legal status of a person born with ambiguous genitalia (khuntha) is crucial for inheritance, marriage, and other rulings. This lesson defines the khuntha and presents the primary method for resolving gender ambiguity: observing the source of urination. The Hanafi school relies on a prophetic hadith and the practice of the Companions to establish this clear, practical rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal person
Recognize that this passage addresses a specific category: a newborn with both male and female genitalia.
2
State the default ruling
The khuntha is initially ambiguous; the rule is to determine gender by a physical sign.
3
Examine the primary sign
The sign is urination: if from the penis → male; if from the vagina → female.
This is based on the hadith from Ibn Abbas.
4
Handle the case of dual urination
If both emit urine, the first to release prevails.
5
Trace the proof
The hadith from Ibn Abbas directly links inheritance to the urination source; this is the operative evidence.
The hadith is ahad but accepted by the Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الخنثى
(1) اذا كان للمولود فرج وذكر فهو خنثى (2) فان كان يبول من الذكر فهو غلام وان كان يبول من الفرج فهو انثى (3) وان كان يبول منهما
ضروری نوٹ جس آدمی کے مرد ہونے یا عورت ہونے کا پتہ نہ چلے اس کو خنثی کہتے ہیں۔ اس کو مرد قرار دیں یا عورت ، اس کے مسائل اس باب میں ہیں۔ اس کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کی علامت قوی ہو وہی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ مرد ہونے کی علامت قوی ہو تو مرد ہونے کو ترجیح دیں گے۔ اور عورت ہونے کی علامت قوی ہو تو عورت قرار دیں گے۔ اس کی دلیل حدیث ہے کہ کوئی مزاحم نہ ہو اور کوئی اور صورت نہ ہو تو علامت دیکھ کر فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ فان جاء احد يخبرك بعددها ووعاء ها ووكاءها فاعطها اياه ( مسلم شریف، باب معرفة العفاص والوكاء و حکم ضالته الغنم والا بل ص ۷۸ نمبر ۱۷۲۳) اس حدیث میں علامت بتانے پر لقطہ کا مال دے دیا گیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی صورت نہ ہو تو علامت پر فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔
(1) جب بچہ کے فرج اور ذکر دونوں ہوں تو وہ خنثی ہے۔ بچہ کو عورت جیسی شرمگاہ بھی ہے اور مرد جیسا ذکر بھی ہے تو وہ خنثی کہلائے گا۔
(2) پس اگر ذکر سے پیشاب کرتا ہو تو وہ لڑکا ہے اور اگر فرج سے پیشاب کرتی ہو تو وہ لڑکی ہے۔ علامت تو دونوں قسم کی ہیں تو جس عضو سے پیشاب کرے وہی شمار کیا جائے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله سئل عن مولود ولد له قبل وذكر من اين يورث فقال النبي يورث من حيث يبول (الف) سنن لیتی، باب میراث الخنثی، ج سادس ص ۳۲۸ نمبر ۱۲۵۱۸ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب خنثی ذکرج عاشر ص ۱۳۰۸ نمبر ۱۹۲۰۴) اس حدیث اور اثر میں ہے کہ جس سے پیشاب کرے وہی شمار کیا جائے گا۔
(3) پس اگر پیشاب دونوں سے کرے۔ اور پیشاب ان میں سے ایک سے پہلے آتا ہو تو ان دونوں میں سے پہلے والے کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے گا۔ دونوں سوراخوں سے پیشاب آتا ہو تو جس سوراخ سے پہلے پیشاب آئے گا وہی شمار ہوگا۔ مثلا ذکر سے پہلے پیشاب آتا ہو تو لڑکا شمار کیا جائے گا اور فرج سے پہلے پیشاب آتا ہو تو لڑکی شمار کی جائے گی۔ اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن قتادة قال سألت سعيد بن مسيب عن الذي يخلق خلق المرأة وخلق الرجل كيف حاشیہ : (الف) حضور سے ایسے بچے کے بارے میں پوچھا گیا جس کو فرج بھی ہو اور ذکر بھی ہو تو کیسے وارث ہوگا تو حضور نے فرمایا جس سوراخ سے پیشاب کرتا ہو اس اعتبار سے وارث ہوگا۔
Book of the Hermaphrodite. (1) If a newborn has both a vagina and a penis, it is a hermaphrodite. (2) If it urinates from the penis, it is a boy; if it urinates from the vagina, it is a girl. (3) If it urinates from both... Necessary note: A person whose gender is not known is called khuntha. The rule is that whichever sign is stronger will be considered. If the sign of maleness is stronger, male is given precedence; if the sign of femaleness is stronger, female is declared. The proof is the hadith: 'If someone comes to you and informs you of its number, container, and string, give it to him' (Muslim). From this, a decision is made by sign. (1) When a child has both vagina and penis, it is khuntha. (2) If it urinates from the penis, it is a boy; if from the vagina, a girl. The hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet was asked about a child born with both a vagina and a penis: from where does it inherit? He said: 'It inherits from where it urinates.' (Sunan [illegible], Book of Inheritance of the Hermaphrodite; Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq). (3) If it urinates from both, and urine comes first from one of them, it is attributed to the one that comes first. For example, if urine comes first from the penis, it is considered a boy; if from the vagina, a girl. There is an athar from Qatada who asked Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab. Footnote: (a) The Prophet was asked about a child with both vagina and penis: how does it inherit? He said: 'According to the orifice from which it urinates.'
Source pages p. 418

Commentary
This passage from the Book of the Hermaphrodite (Khuntha) defines the term and establishes the method for determining the gender of a person born with ambiguous genitalia. The text begins with three Arabic matn statements: (1) If a newborn has both a vagina (farj) and a penis (dhakar), it is a khuntha (hermaphrodite). (2) If it urinates from the penis, it is a boy; if from the vagina, it is a girl. (3) If it urinates from both, the gender is determined by which one releases urine first. The Urdu commentary elaborates: a khuntha is one whose gender is unclear; the rule is that the stronger sign prevails. The proof is cited from a hadith in Muslim about the luqata (lost item) where the Prophet said if someone describes the container and string, it should be given to him—this analogy shows that signs determine ownership, so here signs determine gender. Then the commentary explains each point: (1) The definition of khuntha. (2) The determination by urination is supported by a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet said a child inherits from the same gender as the source of its urine. (3) If urine comes from both, the first orifice to release urine determines the gender. This is further supported by an athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab. The footnote repeats the hadith on inheritance. The passage thus provides clear rules for a legally ambiguous situation, using evidence from hadith and practices of the Companions.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A hermaphrodite person born with both male and female genitalia, whose gender is unclear.
فرج (farj): Female genitalia (vagina).
ذكر (dhakar): Male genitalia (penis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented, how is the gender of a khuntha determined if urine comes from both the penis and the vagina?
A) The child is considered male because the penis is the stronger sign.
B) The child is considered female because the vagina is associated with the majority of urine output.
C) The child's gender is determined by which organ releases urine first.
D) The child remains ambiguous until puberty.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school determines a khuntha's gender by the orifice that first releases urine, as established by prophetic hadith.

Gender Determination of a Khuntha: Precedence vs Quantity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on gender determination via urine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for determining the gender of a khuntha based on urine precedence and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding quantity.

Core Idea
When urine emerges from both orifices simultaneously, Abu Hanifa disregards quantity; the Sahibayn consider the greater volume.

This passage addresses a practical issue in identifying the gender of a khuntha (hermaphrodite) for legal purposes such as inheritance. The primary method is to observe from which orifice urine emerges first. However, if urine emerges simultaneously from both, the Hanafi school splits on whether to consider the quantity of urine. Understanding this dispute clarifies how a crucial status determination is made within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary rule
The passage begins by stating that if urine emerges from one orifice before the other, the person is attributed to that gender. This is the default method.
Supported by the narration of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib.
2
Recognise the scenario of equal precedence
The text then considers the case when both orifices emit urine at the same time. This creates ambiguity and a difference of opinion.
Here, the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn arises.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that quantity is not considered. The person remains ambiguous until other signs appear.
His reasoning is that quantity may depend on the width of the orifice, not a reliable gender indicator.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the person is attributed to the gender from which more urine comes.
This view is often relied upon in later practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبول يسبق من احدهما نسب الى الاسبق منهما [ ۱۶۴٠] وان كانا في السبق سواء فلا يعتبر بالكثرة عند ابي حنيفة وقالا رحمهما الله تعالى ينسب الى اكثرهما بولا
حاشیہ: میں نے سعید بن مسیب سے پوچھا ایسا آدمی جس میں عورت کی تخلیق ہو اور مرد کی تخلیق ہو وہ کیسے وارث ہوگا ؟ فرمایا جہاں سے پیشاب کرتا ہو اس اعتبار سے وارث ہو گا ۔ ابن مسیب کہنے لگے اگر دونوں سوراخوں سے پیشاب کرتا ہو؟ میں نے کیا مجھے معلوم نہیں ۔ فرمایا دیکھو کس سوراخ سے پیشاب جلدی نکلتا ہے۔ پس اس اعتبار سے وارث ہوگا۔
And urine emerges from one of them, so it is attributed to the one from which it precedes [1640]. And if they are equal in precedence, then quantity is not considered according to Abu Hanifa, but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is attributed to the one from which there is more urine.
Footnote: I asked Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib about a person who has both male and female creation, how will he inherit? He said: based on where he urinates, he inherits. Ibn al-Musayyib said: If he urinates from both? I said: I don't know. He said: see from which orifice urine comes out faster, then based on that he inherits.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on gender identification for a hermaphrodite (khuntha). The primary method is to observe from which orifice urine emerges first, and the person is considered to be of that gender. This is supported by a narration from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib. However, if urine emerges from both simultaneously, there is a dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the quantity of urine from each orifice is not considered, so the person remains ambiguous unless other signs appear. The two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that the quantity should be considered, and the person is attributed to the gender from which more urine comes. Abu Hanifa's view is that quantity may be due to the width of the orifice, not a reliable sign. The dispute is intra-Hanafi; the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is typically the view of the Sahibayn in practice, but this text does not specify tarjih.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A hermaphrodite who has both male and female genitalia.
السبق (as-sabq): The precedence of urine emission from one orifice over the other.
الكثرة (al-kathrah): The quantity or volume of urine emitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if urine emerges from both orifices of a khuntha at the same time, what is the ruling?
A) The gender is determined by the orifice with more urine.
B) The gender is determined by the orifice with less urine.
C) Quantity is not considered; the person remains ambiguous.
D) The person is considered male if urine comes from the penis.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, precedence of urine determines gender; if equal, quantity is considered by the Sahibayn but not by Abu Hanifa.

Signs of Femaleness for a Khuntha at Puberty
Ruling on signs indicating a khuntha is female

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five signs that establish a khuntha as female and apply them to determine legal gender.

Core Idea
Any one of five natural female signs definitively establishes a khuntha as female.

In Hanafi law, a khuntha (hermaphrodite) whose gender is ambiguous may be identified as female at puberty through specific biological signs. This passage from the matn lists the five clear indicators that resolve the ambiguity. Understanding these signs is crucial for applying gender-specific rulings in inheritance, marriage, and worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Recognize that the ruling applies to a khuntha (person with ambiguous genitalia). The passage considers signs at puberty.
Khuntha is a legal category, not a medical condition.
2
List the five signs
Read the Arabic carefully: breast development like a woman, lactation, menstruation, pregnancy, and possibility of vaginal intercourse.
These are all exclusively female biological events.
3
Understand the legal consequence
The appearance of any one sign is sufficient to declare the person legally female for all purposes.
It does not require multiple signs.
4
Contrast with male signs
Although not mentioned here, male signs (e.g., beard, deep voice) would lead to a ruling of male. Recognize that the signs are mutually exclusive.
This passage only addresses female determination.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Take a scenario: A khuntha reaches puberty and experiences menstruation. According to the passage, this one sign makes her female.
Menstruation (hayd) is explicitly listed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان ظهر له لدى كثدى المرأة او نزل له لبن فى ثدييه او حاض او حبل او امکن الوصول اليه من جهة الفرج فهو امرأة [ ۱۶۴۳]
Then if breasts like a woman appear for him, or milk descends in his breasts, or he menstruates, or becomes pregnant, or it is possible to reach him from the vaginal side, then he is a woman.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage lists the signs that confirm female gender for a khuntha. These are: (1) development of female-like breasts, (2) lactation (milk production), (3) menstruation, (4) pregnancy, (5) the possibility of vaginal intercourse. Any one of these signs establishes the person as female for all legal purposes. These are natural female characteristics that cannot occur in a male. The ruling is straightforward and does not involve any dispute.

Key Terms
حاض (hada (or haada)): Menstruated; a sign of female gender.
حبل (habal): Pregnancy; a clear female sign.
كثدى المرأة (kuthda al-mar'ah): Breasts like a woman; breast development characteristic of females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a sign that a khuntha is female according to the passage?
A) Beard growth
B) Menstruation
C) Deep voice
D) Urinating from the penis

Key Takeaway
A khuntha is declared female if any one of five female-specific signs appears at puberty.

Khuntha Mushkil: Definition and Legal Status
Definition of khuntha mushkil when gender signs are absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define khuntha mushkil and state the condition under which a person is classified as such in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
When none of the male or female signs appear at puberty, the person is a khuntha mushkil.

In Hanafi fiqh, a person born with ambiguous genitalia is called a khuntha. Gender is determined by the appearance of specific signs at puberty. This passage establishes that if no signs from either gender manifest, the person is classified as khuntha mushkil—a distinct category with unique rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Recognize that khuntha refers to a hermaphrodite, and signs determine gender. This passage covers the case when no signs appear.
2
Recall the signs
The omitted signs include for males: beard, ejaculation; for females: breasts, menses, pregnancy, vaginal intercourse. The source assumes these are known from earlier discussions.
3
Apply the condition
If after puberty none of these signs are observed, the person is not to be treated as male or female but as khuntha mushkil.
This triggers special rules in inheritance, prayer, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان لم يظهر له احدى هذه العلامات فهو خنثی مشكل [۱۶۴۴]
Then if none of these signs appear for him, he is a khuntha mushkil.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage defines the category of 'khuntha mushkil' (ambiguous hermaphrodite). When a person has both male and female genitalia but reaches puberty without any of the mentioned signs (beard, intercourse for male; breasts, milk, menstruation, pregnancy, vaginal intercourse for female), they remain in a state of gender ambiguity. Hanafi law then applies specific rules for such individuals, such as standing between male and female rows in prayer and other intermediate rulings.

Key Terms
خنثی مشكل (khuntha mushkil): An ambiguous hermaphrodite for whom neither male nor female signs have appeared.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Male
B) Female
C) Khuntha mushkil
D) Must wait for further signs

Key Takeaway
A khuntha with no gender signs at puberty is a khuntha mushkil, a distinct legal category in Hanafi law.

Circumcision of a Khuntha through a Slave Girl
Ruling on purchasing a slave girl for circumcision of a khuntha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how a khuntha's circumcision is performed and explain the rationale for using a slave girl.

Core Idea
A khuntha's circumcision is performed by a purchased slave girl to protect the awrah from unlawful looking.

This lesson addresses a unique ruling from Hanafi fiqh concerning the circumcision of a khuntha mushkil (hermaphrodite whose gender is unclear). Since it is impermissible for a man or woman to see the private parts of a khuntha without necessity, the school prescribes a method that avoids such violation. The ruling details the purchase of a slave girl, either from the khuntha's own wealth or from the public treasury, to perform the circumcision, followed by the sale of the slave girl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem
Circumcision is wajib for a male khuntha, but normal methods risk impermissible looking at awrah.
The khuntha's gender is ambiguous, so no free male or female circumciser can be used without violating awrah rules.
2
State the prescribed solution
A slave girl is purchased to perform the circumcision because she is owned and can be commanded, and her awrah is less restricted before her owner.
3
Determine the source of funds
If the khuntha has wealth, he pays; otherwise, the imam buys from bayt al-mal (public treasury).
This ensures the cost is covered without burdening the poor khuntha.
4
Explain the post-procedure disposition
After circumcision, the slave girl is sold and the price returned to the treasury (if bought from bayt al-mal) or to the khuntha's estate.
This prevents permanent ownership of a slave for a temporary need.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The ruling exemplifies the Hanafi principle of sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking means to evil) and protecting awrah.
It also shows the school's attention to practical solutions for unusual cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتبتاع له امة من ماله تختنه ان كان له مال فان لم يكن له مال ابتاع له الامام من بيت المال امة فاذا ختنته باعها ورد ثمنها الى بيت المال.
And a slave girl is bought for him from his wealth, who will circumcise him, if he has wealth. Then if he has no wealth, the imam buys for him a slave girl from the bayt al-mal. Then when she circumcises him, he sells her and returns her price to the bayt al-mal.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage addresses the practical issue of circumcision for a khuntha mushkil. Since it is not clear whether the person is male or female, allowing a man or woman to see and touch the private parts for circumcision would violate the rules of looking at others' awrah. The solution is to buy a slave girl (who is legally owned and can be commanded) from the khuntha's own wealth to perform the circumcision. If the khuntha has no wealth, the Muslim ruler (imam) purchases a slave girl from the public treasury (bayt al-mal). After the circumcision, the slave girl is sold and the money returned to the treasury. This ruling ensures the awrah is protected.

Key Terms
ختنة (khitanah): Circumcision; for a khuntha, performed by a slave girl to avoid forbidden looking.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): Public treasury of the Muslim state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is done with the slave girl after she circumcises the khuntha?
A) She is freed
B) She is kept as a servant
C) She is sold and the price returned to bayt al-mal
D) She becomes the khuntha's wife

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, circumcision of a khuntha is performed by a purchased slave girl to protect the awrah, and the slave girl is sold after the procedure.

Circumcision of an Adult Khuntha: Procurement of a Slave Girl
Ruling on purchasing a slave girl to circumcise an adult khuntha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on procuring a slave girl for circumcising an adult khuntha and explain the procedure when the khuntha has wealth versus when he does not.

Core Idea
When a khuntha needs circumcision, a female slave is procured to avoid unlawful looking—paid from his wealth or from bayt al-mal.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling on a delicate situation: circumcising an adult hermaphrodite (khuntha). Because gender is ambiguous, direct exposure is prohibited. The solution is to purchase a female slave to perform the circumcision, with funds from the individual if able, otherwise from the public treasury. This ruling highlights legal finesse in preserving modesty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and need
The subject is an adult khuntha who requires circumcision. This need triggers the legal mechanism.
The khuntha is a hermaphrodite whose exact gender is unknown, so normal looking is prohibited.
2
Recognize the prohibition
No man may look because the khuntha is considered a woman in that respect, and no woman may look because he is considered a man. Thus, direct circumcision by a person of either gender is impermissible.
The prohibition is to avoid unlawful sexual gaze.
3
First scenario: khuntha has wealth
If the khuntha possesses wealth, a slave girl is purchased from that wealth to perform the circumcision.
The purchase is from his own money, not from public funds.
4
Second scenario: khuntha has no wealth
If he has no wealth, the imam (ruler) purchases a slave girl from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) for this purpose.
Bayt al-mal is used for necessary public expenses when the individual cannot pay.
5
Post-circumcision procedure
After the circumcision is performed by the slave girl, she is sold and her price is returned to the source (either the khuntha's wealth or the public treasury).
This ensures the slave is not permanently acquired; the need is temporary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۶۴۵] (۹) وتبتاع له امة من ماله تختنه ان كان له مال فان لم يكن له مال ابتاع له الامام من بيت المال امة فاذا ختنته باعها ورد ثمنها الى بيت المال.
خنٹی کے لئے باندی خریدی جائے گی اس کے مال سے جو اس کی ختنہ کرے اگر اس کے پاس مال ہو۔ پس اگر اس کے پاس مال نہ ہو تو اس کے لئے امام خریدے گا باندی بیت المال سے، پس جب اس کا ختنہ کر چکے تو باندی کو بیچ دے اور اس کی قیمت بیت المال کی طرف واپس کرے۔
ای خلفی بڑا ہو چکا ہو اور اس کے ختنہ کرنے کی ضرورت ہو تو اس کے ستر کو مرد کے لئے دیکھنا نا جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ عورت ہے۔ اور عورت کے لئے دیکھنا نا جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ مرد ہے۔ اس لئے آخری شکل یہ ہے کہ اگر اس کے پاس مال ہو تو اس سے اس کے لئے باندی خریدے۔ اور وہ باندی اس کی ختنہ کر دے۔ یا اگر اس کے پاس مال نہ ہو تو امام بیت المال سے اس کے لئے باندی خریدے اور وہ باندی ختنہ کر دے۔ اور ختنہ کرنے کے بعد باندی بیچ دے اور اس کی قیمت بیت المال میں دوبارہ جمع کروادے۔
[1645] (9) And a slave girl is purchased for him from his wealth to circumcise him, if he has wealth. But if he has no wealth, the imam purchases a slave girl from the public treasury. When she has circumcised him, he sells her and returns her price to the public treasury. Commentary: A slave girl will be purchased for the khuntha from his wealth to circumcise him, if he has wealth. Then if he has no wealth, the imam will purchase a slave girl from the public treasury. Then when she has circumcised him, he sells the slave girl and returns her price to the public treasury. If the khuntha has become an adult and needs circumcision, looking at his private parts is not permissible for men because he is a woman, and not permissible for women because he is a man. Therefore the final form is: if he has wealth, purchase a slave girl from it for him, and that slave girl should perform his circumcision. Or if he has no wealth, the imam purchases a slave girl from the public treasury, and that slave girl performs the circumcision. After circumcision, he sells the slave girl and deposits her price back into the public treasury.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This ruling addresses the problem of circumcising an adult khuntha. Because his exact gender is unknown, looking at his private parts is prohibited for both men and women. Therefore, a female slave is purchased (from his own money if available, otherwise from the public treasury) to perform the circumcision. Afterward, the slave is sold and the money returned. This ensures modesty and avoids unlawful looking.

Key Terms
بیت المال (bayt al-mal): Public treasury of the Muslims from which funds are allocated for public needs, including the circumcision of a khuntha without means.
ختنة (khitan): Circumcision, here required for the adult khuntha to resolve ambiguity or for hygiene, performed by a female slave.
خنثى (khuntha): A hermaphrodite person with ambiguous gender; in this ruling, an adult khuntha who needs circumcision.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From where are funds taken if the khuntha has no wealth for purchasing a circumcision slave girl?
A) From the khuntha's family
B) From the imam's personal wealth
C) From the public treasury (bayt al-mal)
D) From voluntary charity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides a practical solution for circumcising an adult khuntha by purchasing a female slave from his own wealth or from the public treasury, maintaining modesty at all steps.

Appointing a Caretaker for the Missing Person's Property
Ruling and proof for appointing a caretaker for a missing person's property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a missing person's property and apply the hadith proof to justify the appointment of a caretaker.

Core Idea
The judge must appoint a caretaker to preserve a missing person's property; the wife remains his wife until certainty of death.

This lesson addresses a sensitive legal scenario: a person disappears without trace. Islamic law ensures that his property and dependents are protected. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance through the appointment of a caretaker (wasi) by the judge. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and the textual evidence from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the judge appointing a caretaker for the missing person's property. The ruling is that this appointment is wajib (obligatory) on the judge to preserve the property and fulfill the dependents' needs.
The obligation stems from the need to prevent loss and uphold the rights of the missing person and his family.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith: 'The wife of a missing person remains his wife until news reaches her' (Sunan al-Dar Qutni, Sunan al-Bayhaqi). Also an athar from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar that the wife waits four years and receives maintenance from her husband's property.
The hadith establishes the continuity of marriage, which implies the need to support the wife from the husband's property.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'امرأته' directly indicates that she is still his wife, which carries full rights and obligations, including financial support. Thus, the judge must ensure her maintenance from the missing person's property, requiring a caretaker.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut (a hadith ahad) and zanni al-dalala, but it suffices for a wajib ruling in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may differ on the exact waiting period for the wife (e.g., four years in some opinions). However, the basic ruling that a caretaker is necessary to manage property and support dependents is agreed upon.
The athar from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar about four years is not adopted by the Hanafis for the waiting period; they rely on the hadith for indefinite waiting.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the explicit hadith and the principle of preserving property (hifz al-mal). The caretaker is appointed to protect the property and spend on the widow and orphans, which is a necessity.
The mufta bihi position is as stated; no intra-madhhab ikhtilaf is recorded.

[۱۶۵۰) (۱) اذا غاب الرجل فلم يعرف له موضع ولا يعلم احى هو ام ميت نصب القاضي من يحفظ ماله ويقوم عليه [ ۱۶۵۱] (۲) ويستوفى حقوقه [۱۶۵۲](۳) وینفق كتاب المفقود )
ضروری نوٹ کوئی آدمی گھر سے بالکل غائب ہو جائے تو اس کو مفقود کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی بیوی اور اس کے مال کے کیا احکام ہیں اس کے بارے میں اس باب میں بیان ہے۔ اس کا ثبوت اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن المغيرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله امرأة المفقود امرأته حتى يأتيها الخبر (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۳۸۰۴ سفن للبیہقی ، باب من قال امرأة المفقودا مرات حتی یا تھا یقین وفاته ، ج سابع ص ۷۳۱، نمبر ۱۵۵۶۵) اس حدیث سے مفقود کا ثبوت بھی ہوا اور اس کا حکم بھی معلوم ہوا کہ موت کے یقین ہونے سے پہلے وہ مفقود کی بیوی ہے۔ [۱۶۵۰] (۱) اگر آدمی غائب ہو جائے اور اس کی کوئی جگہ معلوم نہ ہو، اور نہ معلوم ہو کہ وہ زندہ ہے یا مردہ تو متعین کرے گا قاضی کسی شخص کو جو اس کے مال کی حفاظت کرے اور انتظام رکھے۔ کوئی آدمی اس طرح غائب ہو گیا کہ اس کا ٹھکانہ معلوم نہیں ہے اور نہ یہ معلوم ہے کہ وہ زندہ ہے یا مر گیا ہے تو اب قاضی کسی آدمی کو متعین کرے تا کہ وہ اس کے مال کی حفاظت کرے اور اس کی نگرانی کرے اور اس کے مال کا انتظام کرے۔ ایسے آدمی کے لئے قاضی ہی منتظم ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے قاضی ہی کسی آدمی کو متعین کرے گا تا کہ اس کے مال کی حفاظت کرے۔ [۱۶۵۱) (۲) اس کے لئے حقوق وصول کرے۔ ان مفقود کا کسی پر قرض ہو یا کوئی حق ہو تو متعین کردہ آدمی وہ قرض وصول کرے گا اور دیگر حقوق بھی وصول کرے گا اور ان کو مفقود کے لئے محفوظ رکھے گا۔ [۱۶۵۲) (۳) اور خرچ کرے گا اس کی بیوی پر اور اس کے چھوٹے بچوں پر اس کے مال میں ہے۔
ای مفقود کا جو مال ہے وہ مال اس کی بیوی اور اس کے چھوٹی اولاد پر وصی خرچ کرے گا۔ جو کے اس لئے کہ بیوی مفقود کے لئے محبوس ہے۔ اور چھوٹی اولاد کا خرچ بھی ابھی اس کے ذمے ہے۔ اس لئے ان لوگوں پر مفقود کے مال سے خرچ کیا جائے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس وابن عمر قالا جميعا في امراة المفقود تنتظر اربع سنين قال ابن عمر ينفق عليها فيها من مال زوجها لانها حسبت نفسها عليه (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الرجل یعن امرأته فلا ينفق عليها، حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا مفقود کی بیوی اس کی بیوی رہے گی جب تک واضح خبر نہ آ جائے (ب) عبد اللہ ابن عباس اور عبد اللہ بن عمر نے فرمایا مفقود کی عورت چار سال تک انتظار کرے۔ ابن عمر نے فرمایا اس پر خرچ کیا جائے گا اس کے شوہر کے مال سے۔ اس لئے کہ اپنے آپ کو اس کے لئے محبوس کیا ہے۔
Al-Sharh al-Thumayri, Part Two)
420
Book of the Missing Person
Book of the Missing Person
[1650] (1) If a man is absent and his whereabouts are unknown, and it is not known whether he is alive or dead, the judge appoints someone to preserve his property and manage it. [1651] (2) He collects his dues. [1652] (3) He spends from his property.
Essential Note: If a person becomes completely absent from home, he is called mafqud (missing). This chapter explains the rulings regarding his wife and his property. Its proof is in this hadith: From Mughirah ibn Shu'bah, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The wife of a missing person remains his wife until news reaches her.' (Dar Qutni, Kitab al-Nikah, vol. 3, p. 217, no. 3804; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man qala imra'at al-mafqud imra'atuhu hatta ya'tiyaha yaqin wafatih, vol. 7, p. 731, no. 15565). This hadith proves the status of the missing person and also indicates his ruling: that before certainty of death, she is the wife of the missing person. [1650] (1) If a man goes absent and his location is unknown, and it is unknown whether he is alive or dead, then the judge will appoint a person who will protect his property and manage it. If a person has disappeared such that his whereabouts are unknown and it is not known whether he is alive or dead, then the judge will appoint a person to protect and supervise his property and manage it. For such a person, the judge is the administrator, so the judge will appoint someone to protect his property. [1651] (2) He collects his dues. If the missing person has a debt or any right owed by someone, the appointed person will collect that debt and other rights and preserve them for the missing person. [1652] (3) And he will spend from his property on his wife and his minor children. That is, the executor will spend from the property of the missing person on his wife and minor children. Because the wife is confined (waiting) for the missing person, and the expenses of the minor children are still his responsibility; so spending from the missing person's property on them is done. (2) There is an athar: From Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, they both said regarding the wife of a missing person: She waits four years. Ibn Umar said: Spending is made on her from her husband's property because she has confined herself for him. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Bab al-rajul ya'ana imra'atahu fala yunfaq 'alayha). Footnote: (a) He (the Prophet) said: The wife of a missing person remains his wife until clear news comes. (b) Abdullah ibn Abbas and Abdullah ibn Umar said: The woman of a missing person waits for four years. Ibn Umar said: Spending will be made on her from her husband's property because she has confined herself for him.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage introduces the Book of the Missing Person (mafqud). It defines a mafqud as someone who has disappeared with no known location and no knowledge of being alive or dead. The key ruling is that the judge must appoint a caretaker (wasi) to protect and manage the missing person's property. The caretaker is also responsible for collecting any debts owed to the missing person. Additionally, the caretaker must spend from that property on the missing person's wife and minor children. The proof for the wife's status is a hadith from Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said the wife remains his wife until news of death reaches her. An athar from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar states that the wife waits four years, and Ibn Umar specifically mentions that her maintenance comes from her husband's property because she has confined herself for him. This establishes the basis for spending on the wife from the missing person's estate.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A person who has disappeared with no known location and no knowledge of being alive or dead.
وصي (wasi): A caretaker appointed by the judge to manage the missing person's property and take care of his dependents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the first step the judge must take when a man is reported missing with unknown whereabouts and unknown status?
A) Immediately declare the wife divorced.
B) Appoint a caretaker to protect the missing person's property.
C) Divide the property among the heirs.
D) Issue a death certificate after one year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obliges the judge to appoint a caretaker to protect a missing person's property and provide for his wife and minor children, based on the hadith that the wife remains his wife until conclusive news of death.

Rulings Concerning the Missing Person (Mafqud)
Four rulings and their proofs for the missing person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi rulings regarding a missing person and explain the evidence for the wife's indefinite waiting period.

Core Idea
The missing person's wife remains married until certain news; the judge safeguards his property and provides for his family.

When a person disappears without a trace, Islamic law must protect his rights and those of his dependents. This passage from the Hanafi tradition outlines the key rulings: the judge appoints a property custodian, the custodian collects debts and maintains the wife and children, and crucially, the marriage remains valid indefinitely until confirmed death or divorce. The proof rests on the Prophet's ﷺ hadith: 'The wife of the missing person is his wife until news reaches her.'

Guided Path
1
Define the missing person (mafqud)
Identify the precise legal definition: a person whose location is unknown and whose life status (alive or dead) is unknown. This triggers the special rulings.
The definition excludes those known to be alive but absent.
2
Identify the four obligations
List the four rulings: (1) judge appoints a custodian, (2) custodian collects rights due to the missing person, (3) custodian spends on wife and minor children from his property, (4) no separation between husband and wife before certainty.
Each is wajib on the judge or custodian.
3
Examine the primary dalil
Read the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: 'امرأة المفقود امرأته حتى يأتيها الخبر' . Understand how it directly establishes the marital continuity.
This is a sahih hadith, though ahad, making the ruling zanni al-thubut but still binding.
4
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute
Compare the Hanafi indefinite waiting with the Maliki four‑year limit. Note the different proofs: Umar's incident vs. the general hadith.
The Hanafi response holds that the hadith is general and takes precedence.
5
Apply the rulings to a modern scenario
Consider a man who disappears in a conflict zone. The judge appoints a custodian who collects his assets, supports his wife and children, and declares the marriage continues until confirmed news.
Fatwa practice may shift for young women in corrupt times, as the text notes.

مثلا موت کی خبر آجائے یا طلاق نہ ہو جائے اس وقت تک مفقود اور اس کی بیوی کے درمیان تفریق نہیں کی جائے گی۔ او پر ضروری نوٹ میں حدیث گزری۔ عن المغيرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله امرأة المفقود امرأته حتى يأتيها الخبر (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتاب النکاح ج ثالث ص ۲۱۷ نمبر ۳۸۰۴ سفن للبیہقی ، باب من قال امرأة المفقودا مراته حتی یا تھا یقین وفاته، ج سابع ، ص ۳۱ ۷ نمبر ۱۵۵۶۵) (۲) عن على فى امرأة المفقود اذا قدم وقد تزوجت امرأته هى امرأته ان شاء طلق وان شاء امسک ولا تخیر (ب) ( سنن بیہقی ، باب من قال امرأة المفقودا مرات حتی یا تہا یقین وفاته ، ج سابع میں ۷۳۱، نمبر ۱۵۵۶۲) مصنف ص عبد الرزاق ، باب التي لا تعلم مهلک زوجها ج سابع ص ۹۰ نمبر ۱۲۳۳۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں کے درمیان تفریق نہ کرائی جائے۔ کیونکہ وہ مفقود کی بیوی ہے (۳) عن ابن جریح قال بلغني ان ابن مسعود وافق عليا على انها تنتظره ابدا (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب التی لا تعلم مهلک زوجہ ج سابع ص۹۰ نمبر ۱۲۳۳۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ وہ ہمیشہ مفقود کا انتظار کرے گی۔ امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کوئی خبر نہ آئے تو چار سال کے بعد مفقود کی موت کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا اور عدت وفات چار ماہ دس دن گزار کر عورت کو دوسری شادی کرنے کی اجازت دی جائے گی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ عن ابی عثمان قال انت امرأة عمر بن الخطاب قال استهوت الجن زوجها فامرها ان تتربص اربع سنين ثم امر ولى الذى استهوته الجن ان يطلقها ثم امرها ان تعتد اربعة اشهر وعشرا (و)(دارقطنی، کتاب النکاح، ج ثالث ص ۲۱۷، نمبر ۳۸۰۳ سنن بیہقی ، باب من قال تنتظر اربع سنين ثم اربعة اشهر وعشرا ثم تحل، ج سابع ، ص ۷۳۲، نمبر ۱۵۵۶۶ار مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب التی لا تعلم مهلک زوجهاج سابع ص ۸۵ نمبر ۱۲۳۱۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چار سال گزار کر موت کا فیصلہ دیا جائے گا۔ زمانہ خراب ہونے کی وجہ سے جوان عورت کے لئے آج کل اسی پر فتوی دیتے ہیں۔
Book of the Missing Person. (1) When a man is absent, his location is unknown, and it is not known whether he is alive or dead, the judge appoints someone to preserve his property and manage it. (2) He will collect his rights. (3) He will spend on his wife and minor children from his property. (4) And separation will not be made between him and his wife. Necessary note: When a person is completely absent from home, he is called mafqud. The rulings regarding his wife and property are explained in this chapter. Its proof is in this hadith: From Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: The Prophet ﷺ said: 'The wife of the missing person is his wife until news reaches her.' (Daraqutni, etc.) This hadith proves the existence of mafqud and its ruling that before certainty of death, she is the missing person's wife. (1) If a man is absent, his location is unknown, and it is not known whether he is alive or dead, then the judge will appoint a person to preserve his property and manage it. (2) He will collect rights due to him. If the missing person has a debt on someone or a right, the appointed person will collect that debt and other rights and preserve them for the missing person. (3) And he will spend on his wife and his minor children from his property. The appointed person will spend the missing person's property on his wife and minor children, because the wife is confined for the missing person, and the maintenance of minor children is his responsibility. So spending from his property on them is done. There is an athar from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar both regarding the wife of the missing person: she waits four years. Ibn Umar said: 'Spend on her during that time from her husband's property because she has confined herself for him.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar shows that spending on the wife from the missing person's property is done. (4) Separation will not be made between the missing person and his wife. Unless a decisive matter occurs, such as news of death or divorce, separation will not be made. In the necessary note, the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah passed. Also from Ali regarding the wife of the missing person: if he returns and his wife has married, she is his wife; if he wishes he may divorce, if he wishes he may keep her, and she has no choice. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) This athar shows that separation should not be made between them because she is the missing person's wife. Also from Ibn Jurayj: It reached me that Ibn Mas'ud agreed with Ali that she waits for him forever. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) This athar shows that she waits for the missing person forever. Imam Malik says: If no news comes, after four years the missing person's death is decreed, and after observing the waiting period of four months and ten days, the woman is permitted to marry another. His proof is the athar from Abu Uthman: A woman came to Umar ibn al-Khattab whose husband had been carried off by jinn. He ordered her to wait four years, then ordered the guardian of the one whom the jinn had carried off to divorce her, then ordered her to observe a waiting period of four months and ten days. (Daraqutni, etc.) This athar shows that after four years, death is decreed. Due to corrupt times, fatwa is given on this for a young woman today. (End of translation)
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the missing person (mafqud), a person whose whereabouts and life status are unknown. The text begins by establishing the definition and the foundational ruling from the hadith of Mughirah ibn Shu'bah: the wife remains married until certain news. The four numbered points are the core Hanafi rulings. First, the judge appoints a custodian for his property, because the judge is the administrator for those without a guardian. Second, the custodian collects debts and rights due to the missing person. Third, the custodian spends on the wife and minor children from his property. The wife's confinement and the children's dependency justify this. An athar from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar supports spending on the wife. Fourth, no separation is made between the missing person and his wife as long as his life is uncertain. Additional athar from Ali and Ibn Mas'ud emphasize that the marriage continues indefinitely. The text then presents Imam Malik's view, which allows a four-year waiting period followed by a decree of death and remarriage, citing an incident from Umar's time. The commentator notes that in current times, due to societal corruption, some give fatwa on Imam Malik's view for young women. However, the Hanafi position as derived from the hadith is that the wife remains married until confirmed death or divorce.

Key Terms
مفقود (mafqud): A person who has disappeared without any knowledge of his location or whether he is alive or dead.
نصب القاضي (nasaba al-qadi): The judge appoints a custodian (qayyim or wasi) to manage the missing person's property and affairs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the status of the missing person's wife before confirmed news of death?
A) She is divorced after four years.
B) She remains married and must wait indefinitely.
C) She may remarry after four months and ten days.
D) The judge automatically separates them.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that the missing person's marriage continues indefinitely, his property is managed by a court-appointed custodian, and his wife and children receive maintenance from his estate until confirmed news of his fate.

Reward for Returning a Runaway Slave
Ruling with proofs from hadith and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the reward for returning a runaway slave from different distances and explain the evidence from hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Full reward of forty dirhams for three days' travel; proportional for less.

This passage presents a well-defined fiqh ruling on the compensation (ju'l) due to someone who returns a runaway slave. While a hadith mentions ten dirhams for slaves found in the Haram, the Hanafi school relies on stronger athar from Ibn Masud and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz to determine the amount for longer distances. You will learn how the school reconciles these proofs and applies a proportional scale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, identify the act: returning a runaway slave to his master. The ruling: the master must pay a reward (ju'l). The hukm level: wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Ibn Umar about the reward being ten dirhams in the Haram, and athar from Ibn Masud (forty dirhams) and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz (proportional per day).
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith establishes the principle of reward (ju'l) for returning a runaway slave. The athar specify the amounts for different distances. The command implies obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is a difference between the hadith (ten dirhams for Haram) and the athar (forty dirhams for three days). Hanafis reconcile by limiting the hadith to the Haram and applying the athar for general cases.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position relies on the athar from Ibn Masud and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, which are considered more specific to the distance. The mufta bihi is forty dirhams for three days, proportional for less.

قضى في يوم بدينار وفي يومين دينارين وفي ثلاثة ايام ثلاثة دنانير فمازاد على الاربعة فليس له الا اربعة (مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الجعل فی الآبق ج ثامن ص ۲۰۸ نمبر ۱۴۹۱۲) اس اثر میں ایک دن کی مسافت سے لایا تو ایک دینار دینے کا فیصلہ کیا اور ایک دینار دس درہم کا ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے چار دینا ر چالیس درہم کے ہوئے۔ اور دو دن کی مسافت سے لایا تو دو دینار ملیں گے۔ اور تین دن کی مسافت سے لایا تو تین دینار ملیں گے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تین سے کم کی مسافت سے بلایا تو اسی کے حساب سے انعام دیا جائے گا۔
If the slave runs away and a man returns him to his master from a distance of three days or more, then he has upon him a reward, and it is forty dirhams. And if he returns him from less than that, then it is in proportion. [And it is necessary note: the slave runs away from the possession of the master, this is called ibaq. The person who brings him will receive a reward called ju'l. Its proof is in this hadith: From Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged regarding the runaway slave found in the Haram with ten dirhams. From this hadith it is known that if a runaway slave is brought from the Haram, ten dirhams will be given. From this, the reward is proven. [1657] (1) If a slave runs away and a person brings him to his master from a distance of three days or more, then for him is his wage, and it is forty dirhams. And if he returns him from less distance, then it will be in proportion. There is difference in the athar. Some athar indicate that forty should be given, therefore according to the Hanafis, if brought from three days distance or more, forty dirhams are given; if from less, it is given in proportion. The hadith of giving ten dirhams has passed in the necessary note. He said: The Messenger of Allah judged regarding the runaway slave found in the Haram with ten dirhams. And for forty dirhams, there is this athar: From Abu Amr and al-Shaybani: I found runaway slaves at al-Ain, so I came to Abdullah ibn Masud and mentioned that to him. He said: The wage and the booty. I said: This is the wage, so what is the booty? He said: Forty dirhams for each head. This athar mentions giving forty dirhams. And giving proportionally is mentioned in this athar: Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz judged: for one day, one dinar; for two days, two dinars; for three days, three dinars; and what exceeds four, he only has four. In this athar, from one day's distance he judged to give one dinar, and one dinar equals ten dirhams, so four dinars are forty dirhams. So if brought from two days, two dinars; from three days, three dinars. From this it is known that if brought from less than three days, the reward is given in proportion.]
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the reward (ju'l) for returning a runaway slave. The author first states the ruling: if a slave runs away and someone returns him to his master from a distance of three days' travel or more, the retriever is entitled to a reward of forty dirhams. If the distance is less, the reward is proportional to the distance. The author then provides evidence from hadith and athar (sayings of Companions and Successors). A hadith from Ibn Umar establishes that the Prophet (peace be upon him) fixed the reward at ten dirhams for a runaway found in the Haram (sacred precincts of Mecca). But the Hanafi school relies on an athar from Abdullah ibn Masud that gives forty dirhams for each slave from a distance. Another athar from Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz shows proportional calculation: one dinar per day of travel, with a maximum of four dinars (since one dinar = ten dirhams, four dinars = forty dirhams). Thus, for a three-day journey, the reward is forty dirhams; for less, it is calculated accordingly. The Hanafi position is clear: full reward for three days or more, proportional for less.

Key Terms
اباق (ibaq): The act of a slave running away from his master.
جعل (ju'l): The reward or payment given to a person for returning a runaway slave.
مسيرة ثلثة ايام (masirat thalathati ayyam): A distance of three days' travel, which is the threshold for the full reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Ten dirhams
B) Forty dirhams
C) Proportional to the slave's value
D) One dinar per day

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school sets the reward for returning a runaway slave at forty dirhams for a three-day journey or more, with proportional payment for shorter distances, based on athar from Ibn Masud and Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz.

Reward Capped at Slave's Value Minus One Dirham
Ruling with proof on capping reward at slave's value minus one dirham.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the reward for returning a slave when its value is less than forty dirhams, and explain the rationale for capping the reward at value minus one dirham.

Core Idea
The reward for returning a slave is capped at its value minus one dirham to prevent undue hardship to the master.

This passage addresses a specific edge case: what if the slave's market value is less than the standard reward of forty dirhams? The Hanafi school, through istihsan, reduces the reward to the slave's value minus one dirham. This balances the interests of the retriever (who deserves compensation) and the master (who should not pay more than the slave's worth). However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, insisting on the full forty dirhams based on the literal athar. Understanding this dispute illustrates how Hanafi jurists weigh textual evidence against legal reasoning (talil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
When a slave's value is less than 40 dirhams, the retriever is awarded the slave's value minus one dirham (e.g., 30 dirhams → 29 dirhams).
This is the majority Hanafi position stated in the matn.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The ruling is based on istihsan: giving the full 40 dirhams when the slave is worth less would impose excessive hardship on the master. Subtracting one dirham ensures the retriever still gets a reward while the master is not burdened beyond the slave's value.
The one dirham is kept as a token reward to preserve the retriever's right.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the full 40 dirhams must be paid regardless of the slave's value, because the athar (tradition) explicitly mentions forty dirhams for a three-day journey.
This is a dispute within the Hanafi school itself.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference is the amount the retriever receives: under the majority, it's value minus one; under Abu Yusuf, it's always 40.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كانت قیمته اقل من اربعين درهما قضى له بقيمته الا درهما [ اگر غلام کی قیمت چالیس درہم سے کم ہو تو لوٹانے والے کے لئے فیصلہ کریں گے اس کی قیمت کا مگر ایک درہم ۔ مثلا غلام کی قیمت تیں درہم تھی اور واپس لانے والے نے تین دن کی مسافت سے واپس لایا ہے اس لئے اس کو چالیس درہم ملنے چاہئے ۔ اب اگر مالک پر چالیس درہم لازم کرتے ہیں تو تمیں درہم کے غلام کے بدلے چالیس درہم دینا پڑ رہا ہے جو مالک پر بوجھ ہوگا۔ اس لئے غلام کی جتنی قیمت ہے اس سے ایک درہم کم کر کے فیصلہ کریں گے۔ مثلا انتیس درہم دلوائیں گے تا کہ واپس لانے والے کو بھی مزدوری مل جائے اور مالک کو بھی غلام کی قیمت سے زیادہ بوجھ نہ پڑے۔ قا امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اثر میں چالیس درہم کا تذکرہ ہے اس لئے تین دن کی مسافت سے لایا ہے تو چالیس درہم ہی لازم کریں گے۔
And if his value is less than forty dirhams, he is judged to have its value except one dirham. [If the slave's value is less than forty dirhams, then for the returner we will judge his value except one dirham. For example, the slave's value is thirty dirhams and the returner brought him from a three-day journey, so he should receive forty dirhams. Now, if we obligate forty dirhams upon the master, then for a slave worth thirty dirhams, he pays forty, which is a burden. Therefore, we judge based on the slave's value minus one dirham. For example, we make him pay twenty-nine dirhams, so that the returner gets some wage and the master is not burdened beyond the slave's value. Imam Abu Yusuf says: In the athar, mention is of forty dirhams, so for a three-day journey, we obligate forty dirhams.]
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage addresses an edge case in the reward for returning a runaway slave: when the slave's market value is less than the standard reward of forty dirhams. The author presents the Hanafi ruling: the reward is capped at the slave's value minus one dirham. For example, if the slave is worth thirty dirhams and the returner brings him from a three-day journey, instead of forty dirhams, he receives twenty-nine dirhams. This prevents the master from being burdened beyond the value of the slave. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that the athar explicitly states forty dirhams, so he would apply the full forty dirhams regardless. The author does not explicitly choose between the two, but the majority Hanafi position is the one stated in the matn (cap at value minus one).

Key Terms
قیمت (qimat): The market value of the slave at the time of return.
الا درهما (illa dirhaman): Except one dirham; meaning the reward is the value minus one dirham.
اثر (athar): A tradition or report, here referring to a prophetic or companion statement about the reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a runaway slave is worth 30 dirhams and is returned from a three-day journey, how much reward does the retriever get according to the Hanafi ruling?
A) 40 dirhams
B) 30 dirhams
C) 29 dirhams
D) 10 dirhams

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school caps the reward at the slave's value minus one dirham to prevent hardship, using istihsan over a literal reading of the athar.
