Master's Liability upon Freeing an Indebted Ma'dhun Slave
Ruling with proof on master's liability upon freeing indebted ma'dhun slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on emancipating a ma'dhun slave in debt and apply the master's liability for the slave's value.

Core Idea
Freeing a ma'dhun slave with debts is valid, but the master must compensate creditors with the slave's value.

This lesson addresses a situation where a master owns a ma'dhun slave (a slave permitted to trade) who has incurred debts. If the master emancipates such a slave, the act is valid because the slave's person belongs to the master. However, to protect creditors from loss, the master becomes liable for the slave's market value, which is distributed proportionally among them. This ruling is grounded in an athar (tradition) from Hammad and other early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the master's emancipation of a ma'dhun slave. The ruling is that the emancipation is valid (ja'iz).
2
Determine the master's liability
The master is liable (damin) for the slave's value to the creditors. This compensates for the loss caused by removing the slave from their reach.
3
Examine the evidence
The text cites an athar: 'Our companions Hammad and others said: If he emancipates him while he has a debt, then the value of the slave is upon the master, and the creditors will sell him regarding what is over the value.' This establishes the principle.
4
Apply the example
If the slave owes 6000 dirhams and is worth 5000, the master pays 5000 to the creditors, who distribute it proportionally. The master compensates only for the value he extinguished.
The slave remains liable for any remaining debt beyond his value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اعتق المولى العبد الماذون وعليه ديون فعتقه جائز والمولى ضامن بقيمته للغرماء [۱۹۹۶] (۲۳) اور اگر مولی نے ماذون غلام کو آزاد کر دیا اور اس پر قرض ہو تو اس کا آزاد کرنا جائز ہے اور مولی اس کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا قرض خواہوں کے لئے۔ پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ چاہے ماذون غلام پر اتنا قرض آجائے کہ اس کی جان اور کمائی سب گھر جائیں پھر بھی غلام کی جان مولی کی ہے۔ اگر چہ اس کی کمائی مولی کی شمار نہیں ہوگی ۔ اس لئے اگر مولی اس غلام کو آزاد کرنا چاہے تو جائز ہے۔ البتہ غلام کی جتنی قیمت ہے قرض خواہوں کے لئے اتنے کا ذمہ دارموں ہوگا۔ اور اتنی رقم مولی کو ادا کرنی ہوگی تاکہ وہ قرض والوں کے درمیان فیصد کے مطابق تقسیم کردی جائے۔ مثلا غلام پر چھ ہزار درہم قرض تھے اور غلام پانچ ہزار کا تھا تو مولی پانچ ہزار قرض والوں کو دے گا۔ اس لئے کے مولی نے غلام آزاد کر کے قرض والوں کو اتنا نقصان دیا ہے (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ قال اصحابنا حماد وغیرہ فقالوا اذا اعتقه وعليه دين فقيمة العبد على السيد و يبيعه غرماء ٥ فيما زاد على القيمة (الف) مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب هل يباع العبد فی دینا اذا اذن له او الحرج ثامن ص ۲۸۶ نمبر ۱۵۲۴۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مولی آزاد کرے تو غلام کی جتنی قیمت ہے اتنے کا ذمہ دار مولی ہوگا۔ اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مولی نے جتنا نقصان کیا ہے اتنے ہی کا ذمہ دار ہوگا۔
And if the master emancipates the ma'dhun slave, and he has debts, then his emancipation is valid, and the master is liable for his value to the creditors. [1696] (23) And if the master emancipates the ma'dhun slave and he has debts, then his emancipation is valid, and the master will be guarantor for his value to the creditors. It has passed before that even if the ma'dhun slave incurs so much debt that his life and earnings are all consumed, nevertheless the slave's life belongs to the master. Although his earnings are not counted as the master's, therefore if the master wants to free this slave, it is permissible. However, whatever the value of the slave, the master will be responsible for that amount to the creditors. And the master must pay that amount so that it can be distributed among the creditors proportionally. For example, if the slave had debts of six thousand dirhams and the slave was worth five thousand, then the master will give five thousand to the creditors. Because the master has caused that much loss to the creditors by freeing the slave. (2) There is proof for this in an athar. Our companions Hammad and others said: If he emancipates him while he has a debt, then the value of the slave is upon the master, and the creditors will sell him regarding what is over the value. (al-Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq, chapter ...). From this athar it is known that if the master frees him, then he is responsible for the value of the slave. The principle of this issue is that the master will be responsible for whatever loss he caused.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a master emancipates his ma'dhun slave who is in debt. The emancipation is valid because the slave's person belongs to the master. However, to protect creditors, the master is liable to pay the slave's market value, which is then distributed among the creditors according to their shares. The text supports this with an athar from Hammad and others, establishing that the master compensates for the loss he causes to creditors.

Key Terms
ضامن (damin): Guarantor, liable for payment.
مأذون (ma'dhun): A slave permitted by the master to engage in trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master frees his ma'dhun slave who has debts, what is the master's obligation?
A) The master must pay all the slave's debts
B) The master must pay the slave's market value to creditors
C) The master has no obligation
D) The emancipation is invalid if the slave has debts

Key Takeaway
When a master emancipates a ma'dhun slave with debts, the emancipation is valid but the master must compensate creditors by paying the slave's market value.

6 min
Remaining Debt Pursued from the Freed Slave
Ruling that remaining debt after slave's value is demanded from the freed slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on remaining debt after the master pays the slave's value and explain the proof from the athar of Hammad.

Core Idea
The freed slave remains liable for debts beyond his value; the master's liability is limited to his value.

In the previous lesson, we saw that the master pays the slave's value to creditors. But does that fully discharge the debt? This lesson clarifies that any remaining balance is still due from the freed slave himself, because he originally incurred the debt. The ruling is supported by a statement from the companion Hammad and other early scholars.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the specific legal ruling: after the master pays the slave's value to creditors, the freed slave is still liable for any remaining debt.
The ruling applies only if the slave is freed after the master pays the value; if the slave is not freed, the debt is covered by the master's payment.
2
Understand the reasoning
Explain the rationale: the slave took the loans himself, so the debt is his personal obligation. The master's payment of the slave's value compensates the creditors for the asset loss (the slave being freed), but does not erase the slave's personal liability.
3
Identify the proof
Locate the evidence: the athar from Hammad and others in al-Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq. The key phrase is: 'If anything remains over the value of the slave, the slave is pursued for it.'
This is a qawl sahabi (statement of a Companion), which is a source in Hanafi methodology.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Show how the phrase proves the ruling: 'the slave is pursued for it' indicates legal pursuit (mutalaba) of the freed slave for the excess. The imperative tone implies obligation.
In Hanafi usul, a direct imperative (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a contextual reason otherwise.
5
Apply the rule to similar cases
Consider a scenario: if the slave is freed without the master paying the value, the slave remains fully liable for the entire debt. This lesson only covers the case where the master has paid the value.
The ruling reinforces that emancipation does not extinguish pre-existing debts.

And whatever remains of the debts is demanded from the freed slave. (24) And the remaining part of the debt will be demanded from the freed slave. Apart from the slave's value, whatever excess debt there is—in the above example it was one thousand—then after the slave is freed, it will be demanded from him. Originally, he took the loans from people, so besides the value, whatever remains will be recovered from the slave, not the master. (2) There is proof for this in the above athar. In the above athar, there is this additional sentence: Our companions Hammad and others said: Then if anything remains over the value of the slave, the slave is pursued for it. (al-Musannaf...). In this athar, it is stated that the excess over the value will be recovered from the freed slave.
Source pages p. 444

Commentary
This passage completes the previous ruling: after the master pays the slave's value to creditors, any remaining debt is still due from the freed slave himself. The reasoning is that the slave originally incurred the debt, and the master's liability is limited to the value of the slave (the asset lost to creditors). The text supports this with the same athar, which explicitly states that any excess is pursued from the slave.

Key Terms
معتق (mu'taq): The freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It is paid by the master

Key Takeaway
The freed slave remains personally liable for any debt exceeding the value paid by the master.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sharecropping with Fractional Shares
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of sharecropping with fixed fraction of produce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding sharecropping with fixed fractional shares, explain their proofs, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of this dispute.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa rules fixed-fraction sharecropping invalid; the Sahibayn permit it based on the Khaybar precedent.

This lesson explores a classical intra-Hanafi dispute on sharecropping (muzara'ah) where the landowner receives a fixed fraction of the produce, such as one-third or one-fourth. While the matn states the positions of the three major Hanafi imams, the commentary provides the prophetic evidence each side uses. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for nuanced fatwa-giving, as the practical ruling can differ based on which view is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
Determine what exactly is being ruled upon: sharecropping where the landowner gets a fixed fraction (1/3, 1/4) of the produce. Then state the ruling of each imam.
The act is muzara'ah with a specific share percentage, not a variable share.
2
State Abu Hanifa's proof
Recall the hadiths cited by Abu Hanifa: the Prophet forbade muzara'ah and ordered leasing, and explicitly forbade mukhabarah (taking land for half, third, or fourth). The severe warning from Jabir (war from Allah and His Messenger) is also part of his evidence.
These ahadith are sahih and apparently general in their prohibition.
3
State the Sahibayn's proof
Cite the Khaybar hadith: the Prophet himself treated the land of Khaybar for half of its produce. This practice (fi'l) is used as evidence that such sharecropping is permissible.
The Sahibayn argue that the Khaybar practice is specific and overrides the general prohibition.
4
Analyze the conflict of evidence
Understand how each side resolves the apparent contradiction. Abu Hanifa prioritizes the explicit prohibitory texts. The Sahibayn prioritize the actual prophetic practice, which they consider as establishing permissibility, possibly as a specific case or by abrogation.
This is a classic case of ta'arud (conflict) between qawl (saying) and fi'l (action) of the Prophet.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: if one follows Abu Hanifa, fixed-fraction sharecropping is invalid, and the contract must be structured as a lease (ijara) or a partnership with variable shares. If one follows the Sahibayn, such sharecropping is valid and enforceable.
In later Hanafi practice, the mufta bihi often adopts the Sahibayn's view due to economic necessity and the strength of the Khaybar precedent.

مزارعت سے روکا اور اجرت کا حکم دیا اور کہا اس میں کچھ حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ج) آپ نے منع فرمایا مخابرہ سے۔ میں نے کہا مخابرہ کیا ہے؟ آپ نے فرمایا کہ زمین آدھے یا تہائی یا چوتھائی کے بدلے لے (د) حضور نے فرمایا جو بٹائی کو نہ چھوڑے اس کو اللہ اور رسول کی جانب سے اعلان جنگ سنادو (ہ) حضور نے خیبر کو بٹائی پر دیا آدھے حصے کے بدلے میں جو اس سے پیدا ہو پھل اور کھیتی۔
Book of Sharecropping. (1) Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Sharecropping for one-third or one-fourth is invalid. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is permissible. Book of Sharecropping. Note: Muzara'ah is derived from agriculture. Its meaning is that land is from one person, and ox or seed from another, and whatever produce results, they divide it half-half or one-third and two-thirds. This is called muzara'ah or mukhabarah. Mukhabarah is derived from Khaybar. The Prophet gave the land of Khaybar on sharecropping, so from that, sharecropping is called mukhabarah. There is proof from hadith. From Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet treated Khaybar on half of what comes out of it from fruit or crop. (Bukhari, no. 2328; Muslim, no. 1551; Abu Dawud, no. 3408) From this hadith, it is known that giving land on sharecropping is permissible. (1) Imam Abu Hanifa said: Farming on one-third or one-fourth is invalid, and the two said: It is permissible. To give the field on sharecropping for one-third grain or one-fourth grain, such that whatever grain comes out, two-thirds is for you and one-third for me, or three-fourths for you and one-fourth for me – giving on sharecropping in this manner is invalid according to Abu Hanifa. His proof is this hadith: It is reported that the Messenger of Allah forbade muzara'ah and ordered leasing and said: There is no harm in it. (Muslim, no. 1549) And in Abu Dawud, it is: From Zayd ibn Thabit: The Messenger of Allah forbade mukhabarah. I said: What is mukhabarah? He said: That you take land for half, or third, or fourth. (Abu Dawud, no. 3407) From this hadith, it is known that the Prophet forbade giving on sharecropping for one-third or one-fourth, etc. (3) In Abu Dawud, there is a warning: From Jabir ibn 'Abdullah: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Whoever does not leave mukhabarah, then let him be given news of war from Allah and His Messenger. (Abu Dawud, no. 3406) In this hadith, if one does not leave mukhabarah, announce war from Allah and His Messenger. And mukhabarah means sharecropping, so sharecropping will be impermissible. The two (Sahibayn) say that giving on sharecropping for one-third, one-fourth, etc. is permissible. Their proof: first is the hadith above: From Ibn 'Umar: The Prophet treated Khaybar on half of what comes out of it from fruit and crop. (Bukhari, no. 2328; Muslim, no. 1551; etc.) Footnotes: (a) The Prophet gave Khaybar on sharecropping in exchange for a portion of whatever fruit or crop comes out. (b) He forbade muzara'ah and ordered leasing and said: There is no harm in it. (c) He forbade mukhabarah. I said: What is mukhabarah? He said: That you take land for half or third or fourth. (d) The Prophet said: Whoever does not leave sharecropping, then announce war from Allah and His Messenger. (e) The Prophet gave Khaybar on sharecropping for half of what comes out of it from fruit and crop.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on muzara'ah (sharecropping) when the share is a fixed fraction like one-third or one-fourth. The matn states: Abu Hanifa rules it invalid (batil), while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule it permissible (ja'iz). The commentary explains both sides with proofs. Abu Hanifa's proof: hadiths forbidding muzara'ah and mukhabarah (sharecropping) with fractional shares, including a severe warning from Jabir. The Sahibayn's proof: the established practice of the Prophet at Khaybar, where he gave land for half the produce. The commentator notes that the term mukhabarah originates from Khaybar. This is a classical ikhtilaf where the Sahibayn prioritize the Khaybar practice, while Abu Hanifa prioritizes the prohibitory hadith. The passage does not explicitly state which position is mufta bihi, but it presents the arguments.

Key Terms
مزارعة (muzāraʿah): A contract where one party provides land and the other provides labor and/or seed, and they share the produce according to an agreed fraction.
مخابرة (mukhābarah): Another term for sharecropping, specifically associated with the practice of Khaybar; often used interchangeably with muzara'ah.
باطل / جائز (bāṭil / jāʾiz): Invalid (batil) vs. permissible (ja'iz) as legal classifications of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding muzara'ah (sharecropping) with a fixed fraction like one-third or one-fourth?
A) It is permissible (ja'iz).
B) It is invalid (batil).
C) It is recommended (mustahabb).
D) It is disliked (makruh).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal ikhtilaf on sharecropping with fixed fractional shares: Abu Hanifa prohibits it, the Sahibayn allow it, and later practice often follows the Sahibayn.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Fractional Share Muzara'ah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sharecropping with fractional shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on muzara'ah with fractional shares, identify the evidence for each position, and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Fractional share muzara'ah is permissible by fatwa, despite Abu Hanifa's original view of invalidity.

This lesson introduces the Book of Muzara'ah (Sharecropping) and presents an important intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differ on whether a sharecropping contract where the worker receives a fraction of the produce (e.g., one-third or one-fourth) is valid. Understanding this dispute illuminates how later Hanafi jurists resolved differences through the principle of 'umum balwa (general necessity) and shows the evolution of fatwa within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: muzara'ah (sharecropping) where the worker's share is a fraction like one-third or one-fourth. Note the two positions: Abu Hanifa says invalid (batil), Sahibayn say permissible (ja'iz).
The act is a contract, not an act of worship.
2
Examine Abu Hanifa's evidence
Read the hadiths cited: Zayd ibn Thabit reported the Prophet forbade muzara'ah and commanded leasing; Jabir reported a threat of war for those who do not leave mukhabarah. Reflect on the strength of these prohibitions.
Note that Abu Hanifa's view is based on specific prohibitory narrations.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's evidence
Consider the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet contracted with Khaybar for half the produce, and the report of Madinan practice. Note that this is a positive proof of permissibility.
The Sahibayn prioritize the actual practice of the Prophet over general prohibitions.
4
Analyze the resolution and tarjih
Understand why the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view: due to 'umum balwa (widespread need), the stricter view of Abu Hanifa is set aside. Notice also that in some transmissions, Abu Hanifa himself considered it makruh (disliked) rather than batil.
The principle of 'umum balwa often relaxes rulings in contracts of necessity.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Contrast the outcomes: under Abu Hanifa's view, such contracts would be void and must be rejected; under the Sahibayn's view, they are valid and enforceable. The mufta bihi is permissibility.
This difference directly affects the legal status of countless agricultural agreements.

كتاب المزارعة
[۱۶۹۹](۱) قال ابو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى المزراعة بالثلث والربع باطلة وقالا جائزة
كتاب المزارعة
وری نوٹ مزارعة ، زراعت سے مشتق ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ ایک آدمی کی جانب سے زمین ہو اور دوسرے کی جانب سے بیل یا بیج ہو ۔ اور جو پیداوار ہو وہ دونوں میں آدھا آدھا یا ایک تہائی اور دو تہائی ہو تو اس کو مزارعت یا مخابرہ کہتے ہیں۔ مخابرہ خیبر سے مشتق ہے۔ اہل خیبر کو آپ نے زمین بٹائی پر دی ہے اس لئے اسی سے مشتق ہو کر بٹائی کو مخابرہ کہتے ہیں۔ حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عمر اخبرہ ان النبي الله عامل خيبر بشطر ما يخرج منها من ثمر او زرع (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب المزارعته بالشطر و نحوه ص۳۱۳ نمبر ۲۳۲۸، مسلم شریف ، باب المساقات والمعاملة بجزاء من الثمر والزرع ص ۱۴ نمبر ۱ ۱۵۵ / ابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی المساقاة ص ۱۲۸ نمبر (۳۴۰۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ بٹائی پر زمین دینا جائز ہے۔
[۱۶۹۹) (۱) امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا تہائی یا چوتھائی پر کھیتی کرنا باطل ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا جائز ہے۔ کھیت کو تہائی غلہ یا چوتھائی غلہ پر بٹائی پر دے کہ جو کچھ غلہ نکلے گا اس میں سے دو تہائی تمہارے لئے اور ایک تہائی میرے لئے۔ یا تین چوتھائی تمہارے لئے اور ایک چوتھائی میرے لئے ، اس طرح بٹائی پر دینا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک باطل ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ۔ زعم ثابت ان رسول الله نهى عن المزارعة وامر بالمواجرة وقال لا بأس بها (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب المزارعة والمواجر ص ۱۴نمبر ۱۵۴۹) اور ابو داؤد میں اس طرح ہے۔ عن زید بن ثابت قال نهى رسول الله الله عن المخابرة قلت وما المخابرة قال ان تأخذ الارض بنصف او ثلث او ربع (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی المخابرة ص ۱۲۷ نمبر ۳۴۰۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا حضور نے تہائی یا چوتھائی وغیرہ پر بٹائی دینے سے منع فرمایا ہے (۳) ابو داؤد میں اس طرح وعید ہے۔ عن جابر بن عبد الله سمعت رسول الله الا الله يقول من لم يذر المخابرة فليوذن بحرب من الله و رسوله (و) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب المخابرة ص ۱۲۷ نمبر ۳۴۰۶) اس حدیث میں ہے مخابرہ نہ چھوڑے تو اللہ اور رسول کی جانب سے اعلان جنگ کر دو۔ اور مخابرہ کے معنی بٹائی ہے اس لئے بٹائی نا جائز ہوگی۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ تہائی ، چوتھائی وغیرہ پر بٹائی پر دینا جائز ہے۔ ان کی دلیل ایک تو اوپر کی حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال عامل النبي الا الله خيبر بشطر ما يخرج منها من ثمر وزرع (ه) ( بخاری شریف، نمبر ۲۳۲۸ مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۵۵۱ را بود او د شریف نمبر حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے خیبر کو بٹائی پر دیا کچھ حصے کے بدلے میں جو پھل یا غلہ پیدا ہو ( ب ) آپ نے مزارعت سے روکا اور اجرت کا حکم دیا اور کہا اس میں کچھ حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ج) آپ نے منع فرمایا مخابرہ سے۔ میں نے کہا مخابرہ کیا ہے؟ آپ نے فرمایا کہ زمین آدھے یا تہائی یا چوتھائی کے بدلے لے (د) حضور نے فرمایا جو بٹائی کو نہ چھوڑے اس کو اللہ اور رسول کی جانب سے اعلان جنگ سنادو (ہ) حضور نے خیبر کو بٹائی پر دیا آدھے حصے کے بدلے میں جو اس سے پیدا ہو پھل اور کھیتی۔
Book of Muzara'ah. [1699] (1) Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Muzara'ah with one-third and one-fourth is invalid, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is permissible. Note: Muzara'ah is derived from agriculture. Its meaning is that the land is from one person and the ox or seed from another, and the produce is shared half-half or one-third and two-thirds; this is called muzara'ah or mukhabarah. Mukhabarah is derived from Khaybar, because the Prophet gave the land of Khaybar on sharecropping. Evidence: Hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet contracted with Khaybar for half of what comes out of it of fruit or crop. This hadith shows that giving land on sharecropping is permissible. [1699] (1) Imam Abu Hanifa said: Cultivating on one-third or one-fourth is invalid, and the Sahibayn said it is permissible. The land is given on sharecropping for one-third of the grain or one-fourth of the grain, so that whatever grain comes out, two-thirds are for you and one-third for me, or three-fourths for you and one-fourth for me. Giving on sharecropping in this manner is invalid according to Imam Abu Hanifa. His evidence is the hadith: Zayd ibn Thabit reported that the Prophet forbade muzara'ah and commanded leasing, and said there is no harm in it. And in Abu Dawud: Zayd ibn Thabit said the Prophet forbade mukhabarah. I asked: What is mukhabarah? He said: Taking land for half, one-third, or one-fourth. This hadith shows that the Prophet forbade giving land on sharecropping on one-third or one-fourth etc. Also in Abu Dawud there is a threat: Jabir ibn Abdullah heard the Prophet say: Whoever does not leave mukhabarah, let him be notified of war from Allah and His Messenger. This hadith says that if one does not leave mukhabarah, then declare war from Allah and His Messenger. Mukhabarah means sharecropping, so sharecropping would be impermissible. The Sahibayn say that giving on sharecropping on one-third, one-fourth, etc. is permissible. Their evidence is the hadith above from Ibn Umar that the Prophet contracted with Khaybar for half of what comes out of it of fruit and crop. And another athar: Abu Ja'far said: There was no household in Madinah of the emigrants except they cultivated on one-third and one-fourth. This athar shows that the people of Madinah practiced sharecropping, indicating its permissibility. In Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad and Muwatta of Imam Muhammad, it is reported that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, giving land on sharecropping on one-third and one-fourth is makruh, not invalid. Muhammad said: Abu Hanifa informed us from Hammad that he asked Tawus and Salim ibn Abdullah about cultivation on one-third or one-fourth, and they said there is no harm in it. Then he mentioned that to Ibrahim, who disliked it. Abu Hanifa used to take the saying of Ibrahim, and we take the saying of Salim and Tawus, and we see no harm in it. And in Muwatta of Imam Muhammad: Abu Hanifa used to dislike that. This shows that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, sharecropping is makruh. Due to general need (umum balwa), the fatwa is on the saying of the Sahibayn.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of Kitab al-Muzara'ah (Book of Sharecropping) from Al-Sharh al-Sameri. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the validity of muzara'ah (sharecropping) when the share of the worker is a fraction of the produce, such as one-third or one-fourth. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such contracts are invalid (batil), while the Sahibayn deem them permissible (ja'iz). The passage provides evidence for both positions. Abu Hanifa relies on hadiths that prohibit mukhabarah (a form of sharecropping) and threaten those who persist with war from Allah and His Messenger. The Sahibayn rely on the hadith of the Prophet's contract with Khaybar for half the produce and the practice of the people of Madinah. Interestingly, the passage notes that in Kitab al-Athar, Abu Hanifa is reported to have considered it makruh (disliked) rather than batil, indicating some variation in transmission. The passage concludes that due to widespread need, the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn, making such sharecropping contracts permissible in practice.

Key Terms
المزارعة (al-muzāra‘ah): Sharecropping contract where land is provided by one party and labor/seed by another, with produce shared according to agreement.
المخابرة (al-mukhābarah): A type of sharecropping specific to Khaybar, often used synonymously with muzara'ah but sometimes distinguished.
صاحبين (al-ṣāḥibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position for fatwa in this passage, what is the ruling on muzara'ah with a share of one-third or one-fourth?
A) It is completely invalid (batil).
B) It is permissible (ja'iz).
C) It is disliked (makruh).
D) It is forbidden (haram).

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position on fractional share muzara'ah is permissibility, based on the Sahibayn's view and the principle of umum balwa, despite Abu Hanifa's original stance.
